<li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">1.2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_American_Canadian" title="Latin American Canadian">Latin American</a></li>
<li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">0.5% <a href="/wiki/Multiracial" title="Multiracial">Multiracial</a></li>
<li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">0.3% <a href="/wiki/Canada_2011_Census" title="Canada 2011 Census">Other</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnic2011d_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-ethnic2011d-2">[2]</a></sup></li>

<p><b>Canada</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:EN-CA-Canada.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/EN-CA-Canada.ogg" title="EN-CA-Canada.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>; <small>French: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[kanadɑ]</a></span>) is a country in the northern part of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">ten provinces and three territories</a> extend from the Atlantic to the Pacific and northward into the Arctic Ocean, covering 9.98 million square kilometres (3.85 million square miles), making it the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">second-largest country by total area</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">fourth-largest country by land area</a>. Canada's southern border <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada–United States border">with the United States</a> is the world's longest bi-national land border. The majority of the country has a cold or severely cold winter climate, but southerly areas are warm in summer. Canada is sparsely populated, the majority of its land territory being dominated by forest and tundra and the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>. It is highly <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanized</a> with 82 per cent of the 35.15 million people concentrated in large and medium-sized cities, many near the southern border. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/List_of_census_metropolitan_areas_and_agglomerations_in_Canada" title="List of census metropolitan areas and agglomerations in Canada">largest metropolitan areas</a> are <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>.</p>
<p>Various <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Canada" title="Indigenous peoples in Canada">indigenous peoples</a> have inhabited what is now Canada for thousands of years prior to European colonization. Beginning in the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">British</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">French</a> established colonies, the first being the <a href="/wiki/Canada_(New_France)" title="Canada (New France)">colony of Canada</a> established by France in 1535. As a consequence of <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Canada" title="Military history of Canada">various armed conflicts</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> gained and lost territory until, by the late 18th century, it controlled most of what comprises Canada today. On July 1, 1867, the colonies of <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> were federated to form the semi-autonomous <a href="/wiki/Canadian_federalism" title="Canadian federalism">federal Dominion</a> named Canada. This began an <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Canada" title="Territorial evolution of Canada">accretion</a> of provinces and territories to the <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a> to the present ten provinces and three territories forming contemporary Canada. In 1931, Canada achieved near-total independence from the United Kingdom with the <i><a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a></i>, except for the power to amend <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Canada" title="Constitution of Canada">its constitution</a>. With the <i><a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act,_1982" title="Constitution Act, 1982">Constitution Act</a></i> of 1982, Canada took over that authority (as the conclusion of <a href="/wiki/Patriation" title="Patriation">Patriation</a>).</p>
<p>Canada is a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, with Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> being the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. The country is <a href="/wiki/Official_bilingualism_in_Canada" title="Official bilingualism in Canada">officially bilingual</a> at the federal level. It is one of the world's most ethnically diverse and <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism_in_Canada" title="Multiculturalism in Canada">multicultural</a> nations, the product of <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada" title="Immigration to Canada">large-scale immigration</a> from many other countries. Its advanced economy is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">tenth-largest in the world</a>, relying chiefly upon its abundant natural resources and well-developed international trade networks. Canada's <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Canada–United States relations">long and complex relationship</a> with the United States has had a significant impact on its economy and culture.</p>
<p>Canada is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> and has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">fifteenth-highest</a> nominal per capita income globally as well as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">tenth-highest</a> ranking in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>. It <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_Canada" title="International rankings of Canada">ranks among the highest</a> in international measurements of government transparency, civil liberties, quality of life, economic freedom, and education. Canada is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">realm</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Francophonie</a>, and part of several major international and intergovernmental institutions or groupings including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">G7</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Eight" title="Group of Eight">G8</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Ten_(economics)" title="Group of Ten (economics)">Group of Ten</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a> forum.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Canada" title="Name of Canada">Name of Canada</a></div>
<p>While a variety of theories have been postulated for the etymological origins of <i>Canada</i>, the name is now accepted as coming from the <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_Iroquoians" title="St. Lawrence Iroquoians">St. Lawrence Iroquoian</a> word <i>kanata</i>, meaning "village" or "settlement".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In 1535, indigenous inhabitants of the present-day <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec City</a> region used the word to direct French explorer <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Cartier" title="Jacques Cartier">Jacques Cartier</a> to the village of <a href="/wiki/Stadacona" title="Stadacona">Stadacona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rayburn2001_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rayburn2001-13">[13]</a></sup> Cartier later used the word <i>Canada</i> to refer not only to that particular village, but to the entire area subject to <a href="/wiki/Donnacona" title="Donnacona">Donnacona</a> (the chief at Stadacona);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rayburn2001_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rayburn2001-13">[13]</a></sup> by 1545, European books and maps had begun referring to this small region along the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">Saint Lawrence River</a> as <i>Canada</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rayburn2001_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rayburn2001-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the 16th to the early 18th century "<a href="/wiki/Canada_(New_France)" title="Canada (New France)">Canada</a>" referred to the part of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> that lay along the Saint Lawrence River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> In 1791, the area became two British colonies called <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">Lower Canada</a> collectively named <a href="/wiki/The_Canadas" title="The Canadas">the Canadas</a>; until their union as the British <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a> in 1841.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Upon <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Confederation</a> in 1867, <i>Canada</i> was adopted as the legal name for the new country at the London Conference, and the word <i><a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a></i> was conferred as the country's title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The transition away from the use of Dominion was formally reflected in 1982 with the passage of the <i><a href="/wiki/Canada_Act_1982" title="Canada Act 1982">Canada Act</a></i>, which refers only to <i>Canada</i>. Later that year, the name of the national holiday was <a href="/wiki/Canada_Day#History" title="Canada Day">changed from Dominion Day to Canada Day</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-buckner-17">[17]</a></sup> The term <i>Dominion</i> is also used to distinguish the federal government from the provinces, though after the <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Canada_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Canada during World War II">Second World War</a> the term <i>federal</i> had replaced <i>dominion</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Canada" title="History of Canada">History of Canada</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Canadian_history" title="Timeline of Canadian history">Timeline of Canadian history</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_years_in_Canada" title="List of years in Canada">List of years in Canada</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Historiography_of_Canada" title="Historiography of Canada">Historiography of Canada</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_peoples">Indigenous peoples</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Langs_N.Amer.png"><img alt="Colour-coded map of North America showing the distribution of North American language families north of Mexico" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1170" data-file-width="1290" height="299" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/330px-Langs_N.Amer.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/495px-Langs_N.Amer.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/660px-Langs_N.Amer.png 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Langs_N.Amer.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Linguistic areas of North American Indigenous peoples</a> at the time of European contact</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Canada" title="Indigenous peoples in Canada">Indigenous peoples in present-day Canada</a> include the <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tis_people_(Canada)" title="Métis people (Canada)">Métis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GraberKuprecht2012_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-GraberKuprecht2012-19">[19]</a></sup> the latter being a <a href="/wiki/Mixed-blood" title="Mixed-blood">mixed-blood</a> people who originated in the mid-17th century when First Nations and Inuit people married European settlers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GraberKuprecht2012_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-GraberKuprecht2012-19">[19]</a></sup> The term "Aboriginal" as a <a href="/wiki/Collective_noun" title="Collective noun">collective noun</a> is a specific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Term_of_art" title="Term of art">term of art</a> used in some legal documents, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_Act_1982" title="Constitution Act 1982">Constitution Act 1982</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">first inhabitants of North America</a> migrated from <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> by way of the <a href="/wiki/Beringia" title="Beringia">Bering land bridge</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and arrived at least 15,000 years ago, though increasing evidence suggests an even earlier arrival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndreaMcGeough2011_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-AndreaMcGeough2011-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paleo-Indian" title="Paleo-Indian">Paleo-Indian</a> archeological sites at <a href="/wiki/Old_Crow_Flats" title="Old Crow Flats">Old Crow Flats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bluefish_Caves" title="Bluefish Caves">Bluefish Caves</a> are two of the oldest sites of human habitation in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rawat2012_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rawat2012-26">[26]</a></sup> The characteristics of Canadian indigenous societies included permanent settlements, agriculture, complex societal hierarchies, and trading networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Some of these cultures had collapsed by the time European explorers arrived in the late 15th and early 16th centuries and have only been discovered through archeological investigations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Population_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous population</a> at the time of the first European settlements is estimated to have been between 200,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dying_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-dying-30">[30]</a></sup> and two million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steckel_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steckel-31">[31]</a></sup> with a figure of 500,000 accepted by Canada's <a href="/wiki/Royal_Commission_on_Aboriginal_Peoples" title="Royal Commission on Aboriginal Peoples">Royal Commission on Aboriginal Peoples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> As a consequence of European colonization, the population of Canada's indigenous peoples declined by forty to eighty percent, and several First Nations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Beothuk" title="Beothuk">Beothuk</a>, disappeared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall1998_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall1998-33">[33]</a></sup> The decline is attributed to several causes, including the <a href="/wiki/Columbian_Exchange" title="Columbian Exchange">transfer of European diseases</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> to which they had no natural immunity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dying_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-dying-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> conflicts over the fur trade, conflicts with the colonial authorities and settlers, and the loss of indigenous lands to settlers and the subsequent collapse of several nations' self-sufficiency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaidlawLester2015_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaidlawLester2015-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although not without conflict, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro-Canadian" title="Euro-Canadian">European Canadians</a>' early interactions with First Nations and Inuit populations were relatively peaceful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> First Nations and Métis peoples played a critical part in the development of <a href="/wiki/Former_colonies_and_territories_in_Canada" title="Former colonies and territories in Canada">European colonies in Canada</a>, particularly for their role in assisting European <a href="/wiki/Coureur_des_bois" title="Coureur des bois">coureur des bois</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voyageurs" title="Voyageurs">voyageurs</a> in the exploration of the continent during the <a href="/wiki/North_American_fur_trade" title="North American fur trade">North American fur trade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller2009j_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miller2009j-38">[38]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Canadian_Crown_and_Aboriginal_peoples" title="The Canadian Crown and Aboriginal peoples">The Crown and indigenous peoples</a> began <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_colonization_of_North_America" title="Timeline of colonization of North America">interactions</a> during the European colonization period, though the Inuit, in general, had more limited interaction with European settlers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> However, from the late 18th century, European Canadians encouraged indigenous peoples to assimilate into their own culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> These attempts reached a climax in the late 19th and early 20th centuries with <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Indian_residential_school_system" title="Canadian Indian residential school system">forced integration</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_Arctic_relocation" title="High Arctic relocation">relocations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> A period of redress is underway, which started with the appointment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Truth_and_Reconciliation_Commission_of_Canada" title="Truth and Reconciliation Commission of Canada">Truth and Reconciliation Commission of Canada</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">Government of Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_colonization">European colonization</span></h3>
<p>The first known attempt at <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization</a> began when <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norsemen</a> settled briefly at <a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows" title="L'Anse aux Meadows">L'Anse aux Meadows</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> around 1000 AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> No further European exploration occurred until 1497, when Italian seafarer <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a> explored and claimed Canada's <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic coast</a> in the name of King <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Then <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_people" title="Basque people">Basque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese</a> mariners established seasonal whaling and fishing outposts along the Atlantic coast in the early 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hornsby_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-hornsby-46">[46]</a></sup> In 1534, French explorer <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Cartier" title="Jacques Cartier">Jacques Cartier</a> explored the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">Gulf of Saint Lawrence</a> where, on July 24, he planted a 10-metre (33 ft) cross bearing the words "Long Live the King of France" and took possession of the territory <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> in the name of <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">King Francis I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In general the settlements appear to have been short-lived, possibly due to the similarity of outputs producible in Scandinavia and northern Canada and the problems of navigating trade routes at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1583, Sir <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Gilbert" title="Humphrey Gilbert">Humphrey Gilbert</a>, by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_prerogative" title="Royal prerogative">royal prerogative</a> of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Queen Elizabeth I</a>, founded <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. John's, Newfoundland and Labrador">St. John's, Newfoundland</a>, as the first North American <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">English colony</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> French explorer <a href="/wiki/Samuel_de_Champlain" title="Samuel de Champlain">Samuel de Champlain</a> arrived in 1603 and established the first permanent European settlements at <a href="/wiki/Port_Royal,_Annapolis_County,_Nova_Scotia" title="Port Royal, Annapolis County, Nova Scotia">Port Royal</a> (in 1605) and <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec City</a> (in 1608).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Among the <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">colonists</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">Canadiens</a></i> extensively settled the Saint Lawrence River valley and <a href="/wiki/Acadians" title="Acadians">Acadians</a> settled the present-day <a href="/wiki/The_Maritimes" title="The Maritimes">Maritimes</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Coureur_des_bois" title="Coureur des bois">fur traders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_and_the_Age_of_Discovery" title="Catholic Church and the Age of Discovery">Catholic missionaries</a> explored the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_watershed" title="Mississippi watershed">Mississippi watershed</a> to <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Beaver_Wars" title="Beaver Wars">Beaver Wars</a> broke out in the mid-17th century over control of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_fur_trade" title="North American fur trade">North American fur trade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_West_005.jpg"><img alt="Benjamin West's &quot;The Death of General Wolfe&quot; dying in front of British flag while attended by officers and native allies" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/220px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/330px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/440px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_West_005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Benjamin_West" title="Benjamin West">Benjamin West</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Death_of_General_Wolfe" title="The Death of General Wolfe">The Death of General Wolfe</a></i> (1771) dramatizes <a href="/wiki/James_Wolfe" title="James Wolfe">James Wolfe</a>'s death during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Plains_of_Abraham" title="Battle of the Plains of Abraham">Battle of the Plains of Abraham</a> at <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The English established additional settlements in <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>, beginning in 1610<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> to the south were founded soon after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hornsby_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-hornsby-46">[46]</a></sup> A series of <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_Wars" title="French and Indian Wars">four wars</a> erupted in colonial North America between 1689 and 1763; the later wars of the period constituted the North American theatre of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Mainland <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> came under British rule with the 1713 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a>, and Canada and most of New France came under British rule in 1763 after the Seven Years' War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Proclamation_of_1763" title="Royal Proclamation of 1763">Royal Proclamation of 1763</a> established First Nation treaty rights, created the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Quebec_(1763%E2%80%931791)" title="Province of Quebec (1763–1791)">Province of Quebec</a> out of New France, and annexed <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a> to Nova Scotia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-buckner-17">[17]</a></sup> St. John's Island (now <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>) became a separate colony in 1769.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> To avert conflict in Quebec, the British Parliament passed the <i><a href="/wiki/Quebec_Act" title="Quebec Act">Quebec Act</a></i> of 1774, expanding Quebec's territory to the Great Lakes and <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> It re-established the <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Canada" title="French language in Canada">French language</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism_in_Canada" title="Catholicism in Canada">Catholic faith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_France" title="Law of France">French civil law</a> there. The <i>Proclamation</i> and the <i>Quebec Act</i> angered many residents of the Thirteen Colonies, fuelling anti-British sentiment in the years prior to the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-buckner-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">1783 Treaty of Paris</a> recognized American independence and ceded British North American territories south of the Great Lakes to the new <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> was split from Nova Scotia as part of a reorganization of Loyalist settlements in the Maritimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newman2016_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newman2016-59">[59]</a></sup> To accommodate English-speaking Loyalists in Quebec, the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Act_1791" title="Constitutional Act 1791"><i>Constitutional Act</i></a> of 1791 divided the province into French-speaking <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">Lower Canada</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Quebec#Canadian_Confederation" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>) and English-speaking <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Ontario#Canada_West" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>), granting each its own elected legislative assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Canadas" title="The Canadas">The Canadas</a> were the main front in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> between the United States and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>. Peace came in 1815; no boundaries were changed. Immigration resumed at a higher level, with over 960,000 arrivals from Britain between 1815–50.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> New arrivals included refugees escaping the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Irish_Famine" title="Great Irish Famine">Great Irish Famine</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a>-speaking Scots displaced by the <a href="/wiki/Highland_Clearances" title="Highland Clearances">Highland Clearances</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Infectious diseases killed between 25 and 33 percent of Europeans who immigrated to Canada before 1891.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dying_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-dying-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The desire for <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a> resulted in the abortive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebellions_of_1837" title="Rebellions of 1837">Rebellions of 1837</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Read1985_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Read1985-63">[63]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Report_on_the_Affairs_of_British_North_America" title="Report on the Affairs of British North America">Durham Report</a> subsequently recommended responsible government and the assimilation of French Canadians into English culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-buckner-17">[17]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1840" title="Act of Union 1840"><i>Act of Union</i></a> merged the Canadas into a united <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a> and responsible government was established for all provinces of <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> by 1849.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The signing of the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Treaty" title="Oregon Treaty">Oregon Treaty</a> by Britain and <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Cession" title="Mexican Cession">the United States in 1846</a> ended the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_boundary_dispute" title="Oregon boundary dispute">Oregon boundary dispute</a>, extending the border westward along the <a href="/wiki/49th_parallel_north" title="49th parallel north">49th parallel</a>. This paved the way for British colonies on <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Vancouver_Island" title="Colony of Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island (1849)</a> and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colony_of_British_Columbia_(1858%E2%80%931866)" title="Colony of British Columbia (1858–1866)">British Columbia (1858)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Confederation_and_expansion">Confederation and expansion</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif"><img alt="Refer to caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="1000" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/220px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/330px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/440px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An animated map showing <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Canada" title="Territorial evolution of Canada">the growth and change of Canada's provinces and territories</a> since Confederation in 1867</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following several constitutional conferences, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act,_1867" title="Constitution Act, 1867"><i>Constitution Act</i></a> officially proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a> on July 1, 1867, initially with four provinces: <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, Quebec, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bothwell_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-bothwell-67">[67]</a></sup> Canada assumed control of <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert's Land">Rupert's Land</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North-Western_Territory" title="North-Western Territory">North-Western Territory</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>, where the Métis' grievances ignited the <a href="/wiki/Red_River_Rebellion" title="Red River Rebellion">Red River Rebellion</a> and the creation of the province of <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a> in July 1870.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> British Columbia and Vancouver Island (which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Colonies_of_Vancouver_Island_and_British_Columbia" title="United Colonies of Vancouver Island and British Columbia">had been united</a> in 1866) joined the confederation in 1871, while Prince Edward Island joined in 1873.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canatlas_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-canatlas-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>To open <a href="/wiki/Western_Canada" title="Western Canada">the West</a> to European immigration, parliament also approved sponsoring the construction of three transcontinental railways (including the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific_Railway" title="Canadian Pacific Railway">Canadian Pacific Railway</a>), opening the prairies to settlement with the <i><a href="/wiki/Dominion_Lands_Act" title="Dominion Lands Act">Dominion Lands Act</a></i>, and establishing the <a href="/wiki/North-West_Mounted_Police" title="North-West Mounted Police">North-West Mounted Police</a> to assert its authority over this territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In 1898, during the <a href="/wiki/Klondike_Gold_Rush" title="Klondike Gold Rush">Klondike Gold Rush</a> in the Northwest Territories, parliament created the Yukon Territory. <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">Saskatchewan</a> became provinces in 1905.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canatlas_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-canatlas-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_20th_century">Early 20th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg"><img alt="Group of armed soldiers marching past a wrecked tank and a body" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="640" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg/220px-Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg/330px-Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg/440px-Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Canadian soldiers and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mark_I_tank#Mark_II" title="Mark I tank">Mark II tank</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vimy_Ridge" title="Battle of Vimy Ridge">Battle of Vimy Ridge</a> in 1917</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Because Britain still maintained control of Canada's foreign affairs under the Confederation Act, its declaration of war in 1914 automatically brought <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Canada_during_World_War_I" title="Military history of Canada during World War I">Canada into World War I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Volunteers sent to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> later became part of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Corps" title="Canadian Corps">Canadian Corps</a>, which played a substantial role in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vimy_Ridge" title="Battle of Vimy Ridge">Battle of Vimy Ridge</a> and other major engagements of the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morton-milhist_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-morton-milhist-73">[73]</a></sup> Out of approximately 625,000 Canadians who served in World War I, some 60,000 were killed and another 172,000 were wounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Conscription_Crisis_of_1917" title="Conscription Crisis of 1917">Conscription Crisis of 1917</a> erupted when the <a href="/wiki/Unionist_Party_(Canada)" title="Unionist Party (Canada)">Unionist</a> Cabinet's proposal to augment the military's dwindling number of active members with <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> was met with vehement objections from French-speaking Quebecers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGonigal1962_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-McGonigal1962-75">[75]</a></sup> The Military Service Act brought in compulsory military service, though it, coupled with disputes over French language schools outside Quebec, deeply alienated Francophone Canadians and temporarily split the Liberal Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGonigal1962_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-McGonigal1962-75">[75]</a></sup> In 1919, Canada joined the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> independently of Britain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morton-milhist_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-morton-milhist-73">[73]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">1931 Statute of Westminster</a> affirmed Canada's independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hail_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-hail-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg"><img alt="Crew of a Sherman-tank resting while parked" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3472" data-file-width="2480" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg/140px-Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg/210px-Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg/280px-Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Canadian crew of a Sherman tank, south of <a href="/wiki/Vaucelles" title="Vaucelles">Vaucelles</a>, France, during the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Battle of Normandy</a> in June 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_Canada" title="Great Depression in Canada">Great Depression in Canada</a> during the early 1930s saw an economic downturn, leading to hardship across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> In response to the downturn, the <a href="/wiki/Co-operative_Commonwealth_Federation" title="Co-operative Commonwealth Federation">Co-operative Commonwealth Federation</a> (CCF) in Saskatchewan introduced many elements of a <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a> (as pioneered by <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Douglas" title="Tommy Douglas">Tommy Douglas</a>) in the 1940s and 1950s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On the advice of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_war_by_Canada#Nazi_Germany" title="Declaration of war by Canada">war with Germany was declared</a> effective September 10, 1939, by King <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a>, seven days after the United Kingdom. The delay underscored Canada's independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morton-milhist_73-2"><a href="#cite_note-morton-milhist-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first Canadian Army units arrived in Britain in December 1939. In all, over a million Canadians served in the <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Canada_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Canada during World War II">armed forces during World War II</a> and approximately 42,000 were killed and another 55,000 were wounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Canadian troops played important roles in many key battles of the war, including the failed 1942 <a href="/wiki/Dieppe_Raid" title="Dieppe Raid">Dieppe Raid</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy" title="Allied invasion of Italy">Allied invasion of Italy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">Normandy landings</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Battle of Normandy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Scheldt" title="Battle of the Scheldt">Battle of the Scheldt</a> in 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morton-milhist_73-3"><a href="#cite_note-morton-milhist-73">[73]</a></sup> Canada provided asylum for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_monarchy" title="Dutch monarchy">Dutch monarchy</a> while that country was <a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat_Niederlande" title="Reichskommissariat Niederlande">occupied</a> and is credited by the Netherlands for major contributions to <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day_(Netherlands)" title="Liberation Day (Netherlands)">its liberation</a> from <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-netherlands_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-netherlands-79">[79]</a></sup> The Canadian economy boomed during the war as its industries manufactured military <a href="/wiki/Materiel" title="Materiel">materiel</a> for Canada, Britain, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912–49)">China</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morton-milhist_73-4"><a href="#cite_note-morton-milhist-73">[73]</a></sup> Despite another <a href="/wiki/Conscription_Crisis_of_1944" title="Conscription Crisis of 1944">Conscription Crisis</a> in Quebec in 1944, Canada finished the war with a large army and strong economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_era">Contemporary era</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alexander-NFLD.jpg"><img alt="Harold Alexander at desk receiving legislation" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="614" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Alexander-NFLD.jpg/220px-Alexander-NFLD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Alexander-NFLD.jpg/330px-Alexander-NFLD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Alexander-NFLD.jpg/440px-Alexander-NFLD.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alexander-NFLD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
At <a href="/wiki/Rideau_Hall" title="Rideau Hall">Rideau Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General</a> <a href="/wiki/Harold_Alexander,_1st_Earl_Alexander_of_Tunis" title="Harold Alexander, 1st Earl Alexander of Tunis">the Viscount Alexander of Tunis</a> (centre) receives the bill finalizing the union of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland</a> and Canada on March 31, 1949.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The financial crisis of the Great Depression had led the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Dominion of Newfoundland</a> to relinquish responsible government in 1934 and become a <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> ruled by a British governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buckner20082ed_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Buckner20082ed-81">[81]</a></sup> After two bitter <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_referendums,_1948" title="Newfoundland referendums, 1948">referendums</a>, Newfoundlanders voted to join Canada in 1949 as a province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada's post-war economic growth, combined with the policies of successive Liberal governments, led to the emergence of a new <a href="/wiki/Canadian_identity" title="Canadian identity">Canadian identity</a>, marked by the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Canada" title="Flag of Canada">Maple Leaf Flag</a> in 1965,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> the implementation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Official_bilingualism" title="Official bilingualism">official bilingualism</a> (English and French) in 1969,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and the institution of <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism#Origins_in_Canada" title="Multiculturalism">official multiculturalism</a> in 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Socially democratic</a> programs were also instituted, such as <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(Canada)" title="Medicare (Canada)">Medicare</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Pension_Plan" title="Canada Pension Plan">Canada Pension Plan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_Canada" title="Student loans in Canada">Canada Student Loans</a>, though provincial governments, particularly Quebec and Alberta, opposed many of these as incursions into their jurisdictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Finally, another series of constitutional conferences resulted in the <i>Canada Act</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Patriation" title="Patriation">patriation</a> of Canada's constitution from the United Kingdom, concurrent with the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Charter_of_Rights_and_Freedoms" title="Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms">Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Canada had established complete sovereignty as an independent country, although the Queen retained her role as monarch of Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bickerton_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-bickerton-91">[91]</a></sup> In 1999, <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a> became Canada's third territory after a series of negotiations with the federal government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the same time, Quebec underwent profound social and economic changes through the <a href="/wiki/Quiet_Revolution" title="Quiet Revolution">Quiet Revolution</a> of the 1960s, giving birth to a secular <a href="/wiki/Quebec_nationalism" title="Quebec nationalism">nationalist</a> movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobertsClifton2005_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobertsClifton2005-93">[93]</a></sup> The radical <a href="/wiki/Front_de_lib%C3%A9ration_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Front de libération du Québec">Front de libération du Québec</a> (FLQ) ignited the <a href="/wiki/October_Crisis" title="October Crisis">October Crisis</a> with a series of bombings and kidnappings in 1970<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_sovereignty_movement" title="Quebec sovereignty movement">sovereignist</a> <a href="/wiki/Parti_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Parti Québécois">Parti Québécois</a> was elected in 1976, organizing an <a href="/wiki/Quebec_referendum,_1980" title="Quebec referendum, 1980">unsuccessful referendum</a> on sovereignty-association in 1980. Attempts to accommodate Quebec nationalism constitutionally through the <a href="/wiki/Meech_Lake_Accord" title="Meech Lake Accord">Meech Lake Accord</a> failed in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sorens_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-sorens-95">[95]</a></sup> This led to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Bloc_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Bloc Québécois">Bloc Québécois</a> in Quebec and the invigoration of the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Party_of_Canada" title="Reform Party of Canada">Reform Party of Canada</a> in the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Quebec_referendum,_1995" title="Quebec referendum, 1995">second referendum</a> followed in 1995, in which sovereignty was rejected by a slimmer margin of 50.6 to 49.4 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court</a> ruled that <a href="/wiki/Reference_re_Secession_of_Quebec" title="Reference re Secession of Quebec">unilateral secession</a> by a province would be unconstitutional and the <a href="/wiki/Clarity_Act" title="Clarity Act">Clarity Act</a> was passed by parliament, outlining the terms of a negotiated departure from Confederation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sorens_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-sorens-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to the issues of Quebec sovereignty, a number of crises shook Canadian society in the late 1980s and early 1990s. These included the explosion of <a href="/wiki/Air_India_Flight_182" title="Air India Flight 182">Air India Flight 182</a> in 1985, the largest mass murder in Canadian history;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_Polytechnique_massacre" title="École Polytechnique massacre">École Polytechnique massacre</a> in 1989, a <a href="/wiki/School_shooting" title="School shooting">university shooting</a> targeting female students;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Oka_Crisis" title="Oka Crisis">Oka Crisis</a> of 1990,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> the first of a number of violent confrontations between the government and indigenous groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Canada also joined the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a> in 1990 as part of a US-led coalition force and was active in several peacekeeping missions in the 1990s, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNPROFOR" title="UNPROFOR">UNPROFOR</a> mission in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" title="Yugoslav wars">former Yugoslavia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada sent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932014)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–2014)">troops to Afghanistan in 2001</a>, but declined to join the US-led <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Iraq" title="Invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq in 2003</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> In 2011, Canadian forces participated in the NATO-led intervention into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_civil_war" title="2011 Libyan civil war">Libyan civil war</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HehirMurray2013_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-HehirMurray2013-105">[105]</a></sup> and also became involved in battling the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State</a> insurgency in Iraq in the mid-2010s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Canada" title="Geography of Canada">Geography of Canada</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Canada" title="Climate of Canada">Climate of Canada</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canada_koppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1278" data-file-width="1170" height="360" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Canada_koppen.svg/330px-Canada_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Canada_koppen.svg/495px-Canada_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Canada_koppen.svg/660px-Canada_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canada_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> of Canada</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Canada occupies much of the continent of North America, sharing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_border" title="Land border">land borders</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a> to the south, and the US state of <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> to the northwest. Canada stretches from the Atlantic Ocean in the east to the Pacific Ocean in the west; to the north lies the Arctic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> is to the northeast. By total area (including its waters), Canada is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">second-largest country</a> in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. By land area alone, however, Canada <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_land_area" title="List of countries and outlying territories by land area">ranks fourth</a>, the difference being due to it having the world's largest proportion of fresh water lakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battram2010da_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Battram2010da-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada is home to the world's northernmost settlement, <a href="/wiki/CFS_Alert" title="CFS Alert">Canadian Forces Station Alert</a>, on the northern tip of <a href="/wiki/Ellesmere_Island" title="Ellesmere Island">Ellesmere Island</a> – latitude 82.5°N – which lies 817 kilometres (508 mi) from the North Pole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Much of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Canadian Arctic</a> is covered by ice and <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a>. Canada has the longest coastline in the world, with a total length of 243,042 kilometres (151,019 mi);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> additionally, its border with the United States is the world's longest land border, stretching 8,891 kilometres (5,525 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the end of the last <a href="/wiki/Glacial_period" title="Glacial period">glacial period</a>, Canada has consisted of eight distinct forest regions, including extensive <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">boreal</a> forest on the Canadian Shield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Canada has over 2,000,000 lakes (563 greater than 100 km<sup>2</sup> (39 sq mi)), more than any other country, containing much of the world's <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> There are also fresh-water glaciers in the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Rockies" title="Canadian Rockies">Canadian Rockies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Coast_Mountains" title="Coast Mountains">Coast Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sandford2012_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sandford2012-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada is geologically active, having many earthquakes and potentially active volcanoes, notably <a href="/wiki/Mount_Meager" title="Mount Meager">Mount Meager</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Garibaldi" title="Mount Garibaldi">Mount Garibaldi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cayley" title="Mount Cayley">Mount Cayley</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Edziza_volcanic_complex" title="Mount Edziza volcanic complex">Mount Edziza volcanic complex</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The volcanic eruption of the <a href="/wiki/Tseax_Cone" title="Tseax Cone">Tseax Cone</a> in 1775 was among Canada's worst natural disasters, killing an estimated 2,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nisga%27a_people" title="Nisga'a people">Nisga'a people</a> and destroying their village in the <a href="/wiki/Nass_River" title="Nass River">Nass River</a> valley of northern British Columbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The eruption produced a 22.5-kilometre (14.0 mi) <a href="/wiki/Lava" title="Lava">lava</a> flow, and, according to Nisga'a legend, blocked the flow of the Nass River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Average winter and summer high <a href="/wiki/Temperature_in_Canada" title="Temperature in Canada">temperatures across Canada</a> vary from region to region. Winters can be harsh in many parts of the country, particularly in the interior and Prairie provinces, which experience a <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a>, where daily average temperatures are near −15 °<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">C</a> (5 °<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">F</a>), but can drop below −40 °C (−40 °F) with severe <a href="/wiki/Wind_chill" title="Wind chill">wind chills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In noncoastal regions, snow can cover the ground for almost six months of the year, while in parts of the north snow can persist year-round. Coastal British Columbia has a temperate climate, with a mild and rainy winter. On the east and west coasts, average high temperatures are generally in the low 20s °C (70s °F), while between the coasts, the average summer high temperature ranges from 25 to 30 °C (77 to 86 °F), with temperatures in some interior locations occasionally exceeding 40 °C (104 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccnRegina_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-ccnRegina-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">Government of Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Canada" title="Politics of Canada">Politics of Canada</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;max-width:332px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:108px;max-width:108px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:139px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="1820" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg/106px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg/159px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg/212px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg 2x" width="106"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a><br/>
<small><a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">Monarch</a></small></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:111px;max-width:111px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:139px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Julie_Payette_-_JSC2009e123567.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2044" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Julie_Payette_-_JSC2009e123567.jpg/109px-Julie_Payette_-_JSC2009e123567.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Julie_Payette_-_JSC2009e123567.jpg/164px-Julie_Payette_-_JSC2009e123567.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Julie_Payette_-_JSC2009e123567.jpg/218px-Julie_Payette_-_JSC2009e123567.jpg 2x" width="109"/></a></div>
