<small><a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General</a></small></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:107px;max-width:107px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:139px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Justin_Trudeau_and_Benigno_Aquino_III_November_2015_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="675" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Justin_Trudeau_and_Benigno_Aquino_III_November_2015_cropped.jpg/105px-Justin_Trudeau_and_Benigno_Aquino_III_November_2015_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Justin_Trudeau_and_Benigno_Aquino_III_November_2015_cropped.jpg/158px-Justin_Trudeau_and_Benigno_Aquino_III_November_2015_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Justin_Trudeau_and_Benigno_Aquino_III_November_2015_cropped.jpg/210px-Justin_Trudeau_and_Benigno_Aquino_III_November_2015_cropped.jpg 2x" width="105"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a><br/>
<small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister</a></small></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Canada has a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> within the context of a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">monarchy of Canada</a> being the foundation of the executive, <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial</a> branches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacLeod16_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-MacLeod16-123">[123]</a></sup> The sovereign is Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, who is also monarch of <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">15 other Commonwealth countries</a> and each of Canada's 10 provinces. As such, the Queen's representative, the <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a> (at present <a href="/wiki/Julie_Payette" title="Julie Payette">Julie Payette</a>), carries out most of the federal royal duties in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The direct participation of the royal and viceroyal figures in areas of governance is limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacLeod16_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-MacLeod16-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forseyp1_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forseyp1-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montpetit_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Montpetit-127">[127]</a></sup> In practice, their use of the executive powers is directed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Cabinet" title="Canadian Cabinet">the Cabinet</a>, a committee of <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Crown" title="Minister of the Crown">ministers of the Crown</a> responsible to the elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_House_of_Commons" title="Canadian House of Commons">House of Commons</a> and chosen and headed by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister of Canada</a> (at present <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. The governor general or monarch may, though, in certain crisis situations exercise their power without ministerial <a href="/wiki/Advice_(constitutional)" title="Advice (constitutional)">advice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forseyp1_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-Forseyp1-126">[126]</a></sup> To ensure the stability of government, the governor general will usually appoint as prime minister the person who is the current leader of the political party that can obtain the confidence of a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a> in the House of Commons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Prime_Minister_(Canada)" title="Office of the Prime Minister (Canada)">Prime Minister's Office</a> (PMO) is thus one of the most powerful institutions in government, initiating most legislation for parliamentary approval and selecting for appointment by the Crown, besides the aforementioned, the governor general, <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor_(Canada)" title="Lieutenant governor (Canada)">lieutenant governors</a>, senators, federal court judges, and heads of <a href="/wiki/Crown_corporations_of_Canada" title="Crown corporations of Canada">Crown corporations</a> and government agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forseyp1_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-Forseyp1-126">[126]</a></sup> The leader of the party with the second-most seats usually becomes the <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Official_Opposition_(Canada)" title="Leader of the Official Opposition (Canada)">Leader of Her Majesty's Loyal Opposition</a> and is part of an adversarial parliamentary system intended to keep the government in check.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canadian_parliament_MAM.JPG"><img alt="A building with a central clocktower rising from a block" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Canadian_parliament_MAM.JPG/220px-Canadian_parliament_MAM.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Canadian_parliament_MAM.JPG/330px-Canadian_parliament_MAM.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Canadian_parliament_MAM.JPG/440px-Canadian_parliament_MAM.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canadian_parliament_MAM.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Parliament_Hill" title="Parliament Hill">Parliament Hill</a> in Canada's capital city, <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Each of the 338 members of parliament in the House of Commons is elected by simple plurality in an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_electoral_district" title="Canadian electoral district">electoral district</a> or riding. <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Canada" title="Elections in Canada">General elections</a> must be called by the governor general, either on the advice of the prime minister, or if the government loses a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confidence_vote" title="Confidence vote">confidence vote</a> in the House.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Constitutionally, an election may be held no more than five years after the preceding election, although the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Elections_Act" title="Canada Elections Act">Canada Elections Act</a> limits this to four years with a fixed election date in October. The 105 members of the Senate, whose seats are apportioned on a regional basis, serve until age 75.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Five parties had representatives elected to the federal parliament in the 2015 election: the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Canada" title="Liberal Party of Canada">Liberal Party of Canada</a> who currently form the government, the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Conservative Party of Canada">Conservative Party of Canada</a> who are the <a href="/wiki/Official_Opposition_(Canada)" title="Official Opposition (Canada)">Official Opposition</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_of_Canada" title="New Democratic Party of Canada">New Democratic Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bloc_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Bloc Québécois">Bloc Québécois</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Canada" title="Green Party of Canada">Green Party of Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cansenate.jpg"><img alt="Canadian Senate chamber long hall with two opposing banks of seats with historical paintings" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="854" data-file-width="1310" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Cansenate.jpg/220px-Cansenate.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Cansenate.jpg/330px-Cansenate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Cansenate.jpg/440px-Cansenate.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cansenate.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Senate" title="Canadian Senate">Senate chamber</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Centre_Block" title="Centre Block">Centre Block</a> on <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Hill" title="Parliament Hill">Parliament Hill</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Canadian_federalism" title="Canadian federalism">Canada's federal structure</a> divides government responsibilities between the federal government and the ten provinces. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_Assemblies_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories" title="Legislative Assemblies of Canadian provinces and territories">Provincial legislatures</a> are <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> and operate in parliamentary fashion similar to the House of Commons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montpetit_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-Montpetit-127">[127]</a></sup> Canada's three territories also have legislatures, but these are not sovereign and have fewer constitutional responsibilities than the provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The territorial legislatures also differ structurally from their provincial counterparts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Canada" title="Bank of Canada">Bank of Canada</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> of the country. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Finance_(Canada)" title="Minister of Finance (Canada)">Minister of Finance</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minister_of_Industry_(Canada)" title="Minister of Industry (Canada)">Minister of Industry</a> utilize the <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Canada" title="Statistics Canada">Statistics Canada</a> agency for financial planning and economic policy development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The Bank of Canada is the sole authority authorized to issue currency in the form of <a href="/wiki/Banknotes_of_the_Canadian_dollar" title="Banknotes of the Canadian dollar">Canadian bank notes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GilbertHelleiner2003_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-GilbertHelleiner2003-138">[138]</a></sup> The bank does not issue <a href="/wiki/Coins_of_the_Canadian_dollar" title="Coins of the Canadian dollar">Canadian coins</a>; they are issued by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Mint" title="Royal Canadian Mint">Royal Canadian Mint</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CuhajMichael2011_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-CuhajMichael2011-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Canada" title="Law of Canada">Law of Canada</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Canada" title="Constitution of Canada">Constitution of Canada</a> is the supreme law of the country, and consists of written text and unwritten conventions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dodek2016_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dodek2016-140">[140]</a></sup> The Constitution Act, 1867 (known as the <a href="/wiki/British_North_America_Acts" title="British North America Acts">British North America Act</a> prior to 1982), affirmed governance based on parliamentary precedent and divided powers between the federal and provincial governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olive2015_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olive2015-141">[141]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a> granted full autonomy and the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act,_1982" title="Constitution Act, 1982">Constitution Act, 1982</a>, ended all legislative ties to the UK, as well as adding a constitutional amending formula and the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Charter_of_Rights_and_Freedoms" title="Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms">Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VishnooShirur1997_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-VishnooShirur1997-142">[142]</a></sup> The Charter guarantees basic rights and freedoms that usually cannot be over-ridden by any government—though a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Section_Thirty-three_of_the_Canadian_Charter_of_Rights_and_Freedoms" title="Section Thirty-three of the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms">notwithstanding clause</a> allows the federal parliament and provincial legislatures to override certain sections of the Charter for a period of five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medal-Viki.jpg"><img alt='Two sides of a silver medal: the profile of Queen Victoria and the inscription "Victoria Regina" on one side, a man in European garb shaking hands with an Aboriginal with the inscription Indian Treaty No. 187 on the other' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="796" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Medal-Viki.jpg/220px-Medal-Viki.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Medal-Viki.jpg/330px-Medal-Viki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Medal-Viki.jpg/440px-Medal-Viki.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medal-Viki.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Indian Chiefs Medal, presented to commemorate the <a href="/wiki/Numbered_Treaties" title="Numbered Treaties">Numbered Treaties</a> of 1871–1921</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Indian_Act" title="Indian Act">Indian Act</a>, various treaties and case laws were established to mediate relations between Europeans and native peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FN_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FN-144">[144]</a></sup> Most notably, a series of eleven treaties known as the <a href="/wiki/Numbered_Treaties" title="Numbered Treaties">Numbered Treaties</a> were signed between the indigenous and the reigning Monarch of Canada between 1871 and 1921.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> These treaties are agreements with the Canadian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen-in-Council" title="Queen-in-Council">Crown-in-Council</a>, administered by <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Aboriginal_law" title="Canadian Aboriginal law">Canadian Aboriginal law</a>, and overseen by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minister_of_Aboriginal_Affairs_and_Northern_Development_(Canada)" title="Minister of Aboriginal Affairs and Northern Development (Canada)">Minister of Indigenous and Northern Development</a>. The role of the treaties and the rights they support were reaffirmed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Section_Thirty-five_of_the_Constitution_Act,_1982" title="Section Thirty-five of the Constitution Act, 1982">Section Thirty-five of the Constitution Act, 1982</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FN_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-FN-144">[144]</a></sup> These rights may include provision of services, such as health care, and exemption from taxation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The legal and policy framework within which Canada and First Nations operate was further formalized in 2005, through the First Nations–Federal Crown Political Accord.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FN_144-2"><a href="#cite_note-FN-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ottawa_-_ON_-_Oberster_Gerichtshof_von_Kanada.jpg"><img alt="Supreme Court of Canada building" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2199" data-file-width="3378" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Ottawa_-_ON_-_Oberster_Gerichtshof_von_Kanada.jpg/220px-Ottawa_-_ON_-_Oberster_Gerichtshof_von_Kanada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Ottawa_-_ON_-_Oberster_Gerichtshof_von_Kanada.jpg/330px-Ottawa_-_ON_-_Oberster_Gerichtshof_von_Kanada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Ottawa_-_ON_-_Oberster_Gerichtshof_von_Kanada.jpg/440px-Ottawa_-_ON_-_Oberster_Gerichtshof_von_Kanada.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ottawa_-_ON_-_Oberster_Gerichtshof_von_Kanada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a> in Ottawa, west of Parliament Hill</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Court_system_of_Canada" title="Court system of Canada">Canada's judiciary</a> plays an important role in interpreting laws and has the power to strike down Acts of Parliament that violate the constitution. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a> is the highest court and final arbiter and has been led since 2000 by the Chief Justice <a href="/wiki/Beverley_McLachlin" title="Beverley McLachlin">Beverley McLachlin</a> (the first female Chief Justice).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson2002_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson2002-147">[147]</a></sup> Its nine members are appointed by the governor general on the advice of the prime minister and minister of justice. All judges at the superior and appellate levels are appointed after consultation with nongovernmental legal bodies. The federal Cabinet also appoints justices to superior courts in the provincial and territorial jurisdictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">Common law</a> prevails everywhere except in Quebec, where <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> predominates. <a href="/wiki/Criminal_law_of_Canada" title="Criminal law of Canada">Criminal law</a> is solely a federal responsibility and is uniform throughout Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Law enforcement, including criminal courts, is officially a provincial responsibility, conducted by provincial and municipal police forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> However, in most rural areas and some urban areas, policing responsibilities are contracted to the federal <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Mounted_Police" title="Royal Canadian Mounted Police">Royal Canadian Mounted Police</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Canada" title="Foreign relations of Canada">Foreign relations of Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Canada" title="Military history of Canada">Military history of Canada</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Canada–United States relations">Canada–United States relations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Public_Domain_Image_of_Canadian_UN_delegation.jpg"><img alt="Pictured from Left to right: C.S. Ritchie, P.E. Renaud, Elizabeth MacCallum, Lucien Moraud, Escott Reid, W.F. Chipman, Lester Pearson, J.H. King, Louis St. Laurent, Rt. Hon. W.L. Mackenzie King, Gordon Graydon, M.J. Coldwell, Cora Casselman, Jean Desy, Hume Wrong, Louis Rasminsky, L.D. Wilgress, M.A. Pope, R. Chaput" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="760" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Public_Domain_Image_of_Canadian_UN_delegation.jpg/220px-Public_Domain_Image_of_Canadian_UN_delegation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Public_Domain_Image_of_Canadian_UN_delegation.jpg/330px-Public_Domain_Image_of_Canadian_UN_delegation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Public_Domain_Image_of_Canadian_UN_delegation.jpg/440px-Public_Domain_Image_of_Canadian_UN_delegation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Public_Domain_Image_of_Canadian_UN_delegation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Canadian Delegation to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization" title="United Nations Conference on International Organization">United Nations Conference on International Organization</a>, San Francisco, May 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Canada is recognized as a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> for its role in international affairs with a tendency to pursue <a href="/wiki/Multilateralism" title="Multilateralism">multilateral</a> solutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chapnick2011a_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chapnick2011a-152">[152]</a></sup> Canada's foreign policy based on international peacekeeping and security is carried out through coalitions and international organizations, and through the work of numerous federal institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SensStoett2013a_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-SensStoett2013a-153">[153]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_peacekeeping" title="Canadian peacekeeping">Canada's peacekeeping role</a> during the 20th century has played a major role in its global image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SobelShiraev2002b_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-SobelShiraev2002b-154">[154]</a></sup> The strategy of the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Canada#Foreign_aid" title="Foreign relations of Canada">Canadian government's foreign aid policy</a> reflects an emphasis to meet the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>, while also providing assistance in response to foreign humanitarian crises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada was a founding member of the United Nations and has membership in the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chapnick2011a_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chapnick2011a-152">[152]</a></sup> Canada is also a member of various other international and regional organizations and forums for economic and cultural affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Canada acceded to the <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Civil_and_Political_Rights" title="International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights">International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights</a> in 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cl.C3.A9ment2016_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cl.C3.A9ment2016-157">[157]</a></sup> Canada joined the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS) in 1990 and hosted the OAS General Assembly in 2000 and the <a href="/wiki/3rd_Summit_of_the_Americas" title="3rd Summit of the Americas">3rd Summit of the Americas</a> in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> Canada seeks to expand its ties to <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">Pacific Rim</a> economies through membership in the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a> forum (APEC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Donald_Trump_and_Prime_Minister_Justin_Trudeau_Joint_Press_Conference,_February_13,_2017.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="651" data-file-width="976" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/President_Donald_Trump_and_Prime_Minister_Justin_Trudeau_Joint_Press_Conference%2C_February_13%2C_2017.jpg/220px-President_Donald_Trump_and_Prime_Minister_Justin_Trudeau_Joint_Press_Conference%2C_February_13%2C_2017.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/President_Donald_Trump_and_Prime_Minister_Justin_Trudeau_Joint_Press_Conference%2C_February_13%2C_2017.jpg/330px-President_Donald_Trump_and_Prime_Minister_Justin_Trudeau_Joint_Press_Conference%2C_February_13%2C_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/President_Donald_Trump_and_Prime_Minister_Justin_Trudeau_Joint_Press_Conference%2C_February_13%2C_2017.jpg/440px-President_Donald_Trump_and_Prime_Minister_Justin_Trudeau_Joint_Press_Conference%2C_February_13%2C_2017.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Donald_Trump_and_Prime_Minister_Justin_Trudeau_Joint_Press_Conference,_February_13,_2017.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Trudeau</a> and President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Trump</a> meet in Washington, February 2017.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Canada–United States relations">Canada and the United States</a> share the world's longest undefended border, co-operate on military campaigns and exercises, and are each other's <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_trade_relations" title="Canada–United States trade relations">largest trading partner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Canada nevertheless has an independent foreign policy, most notably maintaining full <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93Cuba_relations" title="Canada–Cuba relations">relations with Cuba</a> since, and declining to officially participate in the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BickertonGagnon2014_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-BickertonGagnon2014-162">[162]</a></sup> Canada also maintains historic ties to the <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Canada–United Kingdom relations">United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93France_relations" title="Canada–France relations">France</a> and to other former British and French colonies through Canada's membership in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Francophonie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Canada is noted for having a positive <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93Netherlands_relations" title="Canada–Netherlands relations">relationship with the Netherlands</a>, owing, in part, to its contribution to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_in_World_War_II#Liberation" title="Netherlands in World War II">Dutch liberation during World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-netherlands_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-netherlands-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada's strong attachment to the British Empire and Commonwealth led to major participation in British military efforts in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a>, World War I and World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeRouen_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeRouen-164">[164]</a></sup> Since then, Canada has been an advocate for multilateralism, making efforts to resolve global issues in collaboration with other nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Canada_in_the_Cold_War" title="Canada in the Cold War">Cold War</a>, Canada was a major contributor to UN forces in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> and founded the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Aerospace_Defense_Command" title="North American Aerospace Defense Command">North American Aerospace Defense Command</a> (NORAD) in co-operation with the United States to defend against potential aerial attacks from the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a> of 1956, future Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Lester_B._Pearson" title="Lester B. Pearson">Lester B. Pearson</a> eased tensions by proposing the inception of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">United Nations Peacekeeping Force</a>, for which he was awarded the 1957 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> As this was the first UN peacekeeping mission, Pearson is often credited as the inventor of the concept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mays2010_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mays2010-169">[169]</a></sup> Canada has since served in over 50 peacekeeping missions, including every UN peacekeeping effort until 1989,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morton-milhist_73-5"><a href="#cite_note-morton-milhist-73">[73]</a></sup> and has since maintained forces in international missions in <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, and elsewhere; Canada has sometimes faced controversy over its involvement in foreign countries, notably in the 1993 <a href="/wiki/Somalia_Affair" title="Somalia Affair">Somalia Affair</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GuardKandahar.jpg"><img alt="Canadian Grenadier Guards in Kandahar Province standing by road with armoured car" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="604" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/GuardKandahar.jpg/220px-GuardKandahar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/GuardKandahar.jpg/330px-GuardKandahar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/GuardKandahar.jpg/440px-GuardKandahar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GuardKandahar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soldiers from <a href="/wiki/The_Canadian_Grenadier_Guards" title="The Canadian Grenadier Guards">the Canadian Grenadier Guards</a> in Kandahar Province in Afghanistan, pictured, fought with Dutch soldiers against <a href="/wiki/Taliban_insurgency" title="Taliban insurgency">Afghan insurgents</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2001, Canada deployed troops to <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">US stabilization force</a> and the UN-authorized, NATO-led <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">International Security Assistance Force</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KlassenAlbo2013_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-KlassenAlbo2013-171">[171]</a></sup> In February 2007, Canada, Italy, the United Kingdom, Norway, and Russia announced their joint commitment to a $1.5-billion project to help develop vaccines for developing nations, and called on other countries to join them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> In August 2007, Canada's <a href="/wiki/Territorial_claims_in_the_Arctic" title="Territorial claims in the Arctic">territorial claims in the Arctic</a> were challenged after a <a href="/wiki/Arktika_2007" title="Arktika 2007">Russian underwater expedition</a> to the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a>; Canada has considered that area to be sovereign territory since 1925.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>The nation employs a professional, volunteer military force of approximately 79,000 active personnel and 32,250 reserve personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> The unified <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" title="Canadian Forces">Canadian Forces</a> (CF) comprise the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Army" title="Canadian Army">Canadian Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Navy" title="Royal Canadian Navy">Royal Canadian Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">Royal Canadian Air Force</a>. In 2013, Canada's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditure" title="List of countries by military expenditure">military expenditure</a> totalled approximately C$19 billion, or around 1% of the country's GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Following the 2016 Defence Policy Review, the Canadian government announced a 70% increase to the country's defence budget over the next decade. The Canadian Forces will acquire 88 fighter planes and 15 naval surface combatants, the latter as part of the <a href="/wiki/National_Shipbuilding_Procurement_Strategy" title="National Shipbuilding Procurement Strategy">National Shipbuilding Procurement Strategy</a>. Canada's total military expenditure is expected to reach C$32.7 billion by 2027.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Provinces_and_territories">Provinces and territories</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">Provinces and territories of Canada</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Canadian_federalism" title="Canadian federalism">Canadian federalism</a></div>
<p>Canada is a federation composed of ten provinces and three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_(administrative_division)" title="Territory (administrative division)">territories</a>. In turn, these may be grouped into <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Canada" title="List of regions of Canada">four main regions</a>: <a href="/wiki/Western_Canada" title="Western Canada">Western Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Canada" title="Central Canada">Central Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Northern Canada</a> (<i>Eastern Canada</i> refers to Central Canada and Atlantic Canada together). Provinces have more autonomy than territories, having responsibility for social programs such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Canada" title="Health care in Canada">health care</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Canada" title="Education in Canada">education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Social_programs_in_Canada" title="Social programs in Canada">welfare</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Together, the provinces collect more revenue than the federal government, an almost unique structure among federations in the world. Using its spending powers, the federal government can initiate national policies in provincial areas, such as the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Health_Act" title="Canada Health Act">Canada Health Act</a>; the provinces can opt out of these, but rarely do so in practice. <a href="/wiki/Equalization_payments" title="Equalization payments">Equalization payments</a> are made by the federal government to ensure that reasonably uniform standards of services and taxation are kept between the richer and poorer provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<div class="center"><small><b>A clickable map of Canada exhibiting its ten provinces and three territories, and their capitals.</b></small></div>

<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Canada" title="Economy of Canada">Economy of Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Canada" title="Economic history of Canada">Economic history of Canada</a></div>
<p>Canada is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">tenth-largest economy</a> as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a> of approximately US$1.52 trillion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GDP_IMF_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-GDP_IMF-7">[7]</a></sup> It is a member of the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD) and the Group of Eight (G8), and is one of the world's top ten <a href="/wiki/Trading_nation" title="Trading nation">trading nations</a>, with a highly <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalized</a> economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> Canada is a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>, ranking above the US and most western European nations on <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">The Heritage Foundation</a>'s index of economic freedom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> and experiencing a relatively low level of <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">income disparity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> The country's average household <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disposable_income" title="Disposable income">disposable income</a> per capita is over US$23,900, higher than the OECD average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECDBLI_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECDBLI-184">[184]</a></sup> Furthermore, the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Stock_Exchange" title="Toronto Stock Exchange">Toronto Stock Exchange</a> is the seventh-largest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> in the world by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a>, listing over 1,500 companies with a combined market capitalization of over US$2 trillion as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:What_did_Canada_export_in_2014.png"><img alt="Chart of exports of Canada by value with percentages" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="750" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/What_did_Canada_export_in_2014.png/220px-What_did_Canada_export_in_2014.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/What_did_Canada_export_in_2014.png/330px-What_did_Canada_export_in_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/What_did_Canada_export_in_2014.png/440px-What_did_Canada_export_in_2014.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:What_did_Canada_export_in_2014.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tree-map of Canada's goods exports in 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2014, Canada's exports totalled over C$528 billion, while its imported goods were worth over $524 billion, of which approximately $351 billion originated from the United States, $49 billion from the European Union, and $35 billion from China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> The country's 2014 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_surplus" title="Trade surplus">trade surplus</a> totalled C$5.1 billion, compared with a C$46.9 billion surplus in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the early 20th century, the growth of Canada's manufacturing, mining, and service sectors has transformed the nation from a largely rural economy to an urbanized, industrial one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HarrisMatthews1987l_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-HarrisMatthews1987l-190">[190]</a></sup> Like many other <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed countries</a>, the Canadian economy is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service industry</a>, which employs about three-quarters of the country's workforce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> However, Canada is unusual among developed countries in the importance of its <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Primary sector of the economy">primary sector</a>, in which the <a href="/wiki/Forestry_in_Canada" title="Forestry in Canada">forestry</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petroleum_production_in_Canada" title="Petroleum production in Canada">petroleum industries</a> are two of the most prominent components.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada is one of the few developed nations that are net exporters of energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-energy_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-energy-193">[193]</a></sup> Atlantic Canada possesses vast <a href="/wiki/Offshore_drilling" title="Offshore drilling">offshore</a> deposits of natural gas, and Alberta also hosts large oil and gas resources. The vastness of the <a href="/wiki/Athabasca_oil_sands" title="Athabasca oil sands">Athabasca oil sands</a> and other assets results in Canada having a 13% share of global <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a>, comprising the world's third-largest share after <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Venezuela" title="Oil reserves in Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="Oil reserves in Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Canada is additionally one of the world's largest suppliers of agricultural products; the Canadian Prairies are one of the most important global producers of wheat, <a href="/wiki/Canola" title="Canola">canola</a>, and other grains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britton_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-britton-195">[195]</a></sup> Canada's <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Natural_Resources_(Canada)" title="Minister of Natural Resources (Canada)">Ministry of Natural Resources</a> provides statistics regarding its major exports; the country is a leading exporter of <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aluminum" title="Aluminum">aluminum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coking_coal#Coking_coal_and_use_of_coke" title="Coking coal">coking coal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Many towns in northern Canada, where agriculture is difficult, are sustainable because of nearby mines or sources of timber. Canada also has a sizeable manufacturing sector centred in southern Ontario and Quebec, with automobiles and <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">aeronautics</a> representing particularly important industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada's economic integration with the United States has increased significantly since <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automotive_Products_Trade_Agreement" title="Automotive Products Trade Agreement">Automotive Products Trade Agreement</a> of 1965 opened Canada's borders to trade in the automobile manufacturing industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KerrPerdikis2014_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-KerrPerdikis2014-199">[199]</a></sup> In the 1970s, concerns over energy self-sufficiency and foreign ownership in the manufacturing sectors prompted Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau" title="Pierre Trudeau">Pierre Trudeau</a>'s Liberal government to enact the <a href="/wiki/National_Energy_Program" title="National Energy Program">National Energy Program</a> (NEP) and the <a href="/wiki/Investment_Canada" title="Investment Canada">Foreign Investment Review Agency</a> (FIRA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> In the 1980s, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mulroney" title="Brian Mulroney">Brian Mulroney</a>'s Progressive Conservatives abolished the NEP and changed the name of FIRA to <a href="/wiki/Investment_Canada" title="Investment Canada">Investment Canada</a>, to encourage foreign investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada_%E2%80%93_United_States_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada – United States Free Trade Agreement">Canada – United States Free Trade Agreement</a> (FTA) of 1988 eliminated tariffs between the two countries, while the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA) expanded the free-trade zone to include <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britton_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-britton-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Canada" title="Science and technology in Canada">Science and technology in Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Canada" title="Telecommunications in Canada">Telecommunications in Canada</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-116_Payload_(NASA_S116-E-05364).jpg"><img alt='A shuttle in space, with Earth in the background. A mechanical arm labelled "Canada" rises from the shuttle.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1876" data-file-width="2836" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/STS-116_Payload_%28NASA_S116-E-05364%29.jpg/220px-STS-116_Payload_%28NASA_S116-E-05364%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/STS-116_Payload_%28NASA_S116-E-05364%29.jpg/330px-STS-116_Payload_%28NASA_S116-E-05364%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/STS-116_Payload_%28NASA_S116-E-05364%29.jpg/440px-STS-116_Payload_%28NASA_S116-E-05364%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-116_Payload_(NASA_S116-E-05364).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Canadarm" title="Canadarm">Canadarm</a> robotic manipulator in action on <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">Space Shuttle <i>Discovery</i></a> during the <a href="/wiki/STS-116" title="STS-116">STS-116</a> mission in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2015, Canada spent approximately C$31.6 billion on domestic <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a>, of which around $7 billion was provided by the federal and provincial governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the country has produced thirteen <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_country" title="List of Nobel laureates by country">Nobel laureates</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">chemistry</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Medicine">medicine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> and was ranked fourth worldwide for scientific research quality in a major 2012 survey of international scientists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> It is furthermore home to the headquarters of a number of global technology firms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Canada <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_Internet_users" title="List of countries by number of Internet users">has one of the highest levels of Internet access in the world</a>, with over 33 million users, equivalent to around 94 percent of its total 2014 population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">Canadian Space Agency</a> operates a highly active space program, conducting deep-space, planetary, and aviation research, and developing rockets and satellites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> Canada was the third country to design and construct a satellite after the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_program" title="Soviet space program">Soviet Union</a> and the United States, with the 1962 <a href="/wiki/Alouette_1" title="Alouette 1">Alouette 1</a> launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Angelo2009s_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Angelo2009s-209">[209]</a></sup> Canada is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> (ISS), and is a pioneer in space <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a>, having constructed the <a href="/wiki/Canadarm" title="Canadarm">Canadarm</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2" title="Canadarm2">Canadarm2</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dextre" title="Dextre">Dextre</a> robotic manipulators for the ISS and NASA's <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bidaud2012_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bidaud2012-210">[210]</a></sup> Since the 1960s, Canada's aerospace industry has designed and built numerous marques of satellite, including <a href="/wiki/Radarsat-1" title="Radarsat-1">Radarsat-1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radarsat-2" title="Radarsat-2">2</a>, <a href="/wiki/ISIS_(satellite)" title="ISIS (satellite)">ISIS</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microvariability_and_Oscillations_of_STars_telescope" title="Microvariability and Oscillations of STars telescope">MOST</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> Canada has also produced one of the world's most successful and widely used <a href="/wiki/Sounding_rocket" title="Sounding rocket">sounding rockets</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Black_Brant_(rocket)" title="Black Brant (rocket)">Black Brant</a>; over 1,000 Black Brants have been launched since the rocket's introduction in 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> In 1984, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Garneau" title="Marc Garneau">Marc Garneau</a> became Canada's first male <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency#Canadian_astronauts" title="Canadian Space Agency">astronaut</a>, followed by Canada's second and first female astronaut <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Bondar" title="Roberta Bondar">Roberta Bondar</a> in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Canada" title="Demographics of Canada">Demographics of Canada</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quebec-Windsor_Corridor.svg"><img alt="Two-colour map of Windsor area with towns along the St. Lawrence river" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="500" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Quebec-Windsor_Corridor.svg/220px-Quebec-Windsor_Corridor.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Quebec-Windsor_Corridor.svg/330px-Quebec-Windsor_Corridor.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Quebec-Windsor_Corridor.svg/440px-Quebec-Windsor_Corridor.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quebec-Windsor_Corridor.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City%E2%80%93Windsor_Corridor" title="Quebec City–Windsor Corridor">Quebec City–Windsor Corridor</a> is the most densely populated and heavily industrialized region of Canada, spanning approximately 1,200 kilometres (750 miles).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McMurryShepherd2004_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-McMurryShepherd2004-214">[214]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Canada_2016_Census" title="Canada 2016 Census">2016 Canadian census</a> enumerated a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Population_of_Canada_by_year" title="Population of Canada by year">total population</a> of 35,151,728, an increase of around 5.0 percent over the 2011 figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Between 2011 and May 2016, Canada's population grew by 1.7 million people with immigrants accounting for two-thirds of the increase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> Between 1990 and 2008, the population increased by 5.6 million, equivalent to 20.4 percent overall growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> The main drivers of population growth are <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada" title="Immigration to Canada">immigration</a> and, to a lesser extent, natural growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> Canada has one of the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada#Immigration_rate" title="Immigration to Canada">highest per-capita immigration rates in the world</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> driven mainly by <a href="/wiki/Economic_impact_of_immigration_to_Canada" title="Economic impact of immigration to Canada">economic policy</a> and, to a lesser extent, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada#Immigration_categories" title="Immigration to Canada">family reunification</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollifieldMartin2014_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollifieldMartin2014-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BeaujotKerr2007j_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-BeaujotKerr2007j-222">[222]</a></sup> The Canadian public as-well as the major political parties support the current level of immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollifieldMartin2014_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-HollifieldMartin2014-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FreemanHansen2013_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FreemanHansen2013-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rahim2014_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rahim2014-224">[224]</a></sup> In 2014, a total of 260,400 immigrants were admitted to Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-res_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-res-225">[225]</a></sup> The Canadian government anticipated between 280,000 and 305,000 new permanent residents in the following years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> a similar number of immigrants as in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> New immigrants settle mostly in major urban areas such as <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Canada also accepts large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> accounting for over 10 percent of annual global <a href="/wiki/Third_country_resettlement" title="Third country resettlement">refugee resettlements</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada's population density, at 3.7 inhabitants per square kilometre (9.6/sq mi), is among the lowest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> Canada spans latitudinally from the 83rd parallel north to the 41st parallel north, and approximately 95% of the population is found south of the 55th parallel north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD2014_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECD2014-232">[232]</a></sup> About four-fifths of the population lives within 150 kilometres (93 mi) of the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a> border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> The most densely populated part of the country, accounting for nearly 50 percent, is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quebec_City_%E2%80%93_Windsor_Corridor" title="Quebec City – Windsor Corridor">Quebec City – Windsor Corridor</a>, situated in Southern Quebec and Southern Ontario along the Great Lakes and the Saint Lawrence River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McMurryShepherd2004_214-1"><a href="#cite_note-McMurryShepherd2004-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD2014_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-OECD2014-232">[232]</a></sup> An additional 30 percent live along the British Columbia <a href="/wiki/Lower_Mainland" title="Lower Mainland">Lower Mainland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Calgary%E2%80%93Edmonton_Corridor" title="Calgary–Edmonton Corridor">Calgary–Edmonton Corridor</a> in Alberta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<p>In common with many other developed countries, Canada is experiencing a <a href="/wiki/Demographic_transition" title="Demographic transition">demographic shift</a> towards an older population, with more retirees and fewer people of working age. In 2006, the average age was 39.5 years;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> by 2011, it had risen to approximately 39.9 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the average <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> for Canadians is 81 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> The majority of Canadians (69.9%) live in family households, 26.8% report living alone, and those living with unrelated persons reported at 3.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam-238">[238]</a></sup> The average size of a household in 2006 was 2.5 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_238-1"><a href="#cite_note-fam-238">[238]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Canada" title="Education in Canada">Education in Canada</a></div>
<p>According to a 2012 report by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD), Canada is one of the most educated countries in the world;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-239">[239]</a></sup> the country ranks first worldwide in the number of adults having <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">tertiary education</a>, with 51 percent of Canadian adults having attained at least an undergraduate college or university degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd_239-1"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-239">[239]</a></sup> Canada spends about 5.3% of its <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> on education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> The country invests heavily in tertiary education (more than 20 000 USD per student).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 89 percent of adults aged 25 to 64 have earned the equivalent of a high-school degree, compared to an OECD average of 75 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECDBLI_184-1"><a href="#cite_note-OECDBLI-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the adoption of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Section_Twenty-three_of_the_Canadian_Charter_of_Rights_and_Freedoms" title="Section Twenty-three of the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms">section 23</a> of the Constitution Act, 1982, education in both <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> has been available in most places across Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Epstein2008_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Epstein2008-242">[242]</a></sup> Canadian provinces and territories are <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Canada" title="Education in Canada">responsible for education provision</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MontesinosVela2013_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-MontesinosVela2013-243">[243]</a></sup> The mandatory school age ranges between 5–7 to 16–18 years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> contributing to an adult literacy rate of 99 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-107">[107]</a></sup> In 2002, 43 percent of Canadians aged 25 to 64 possessed a post-secondary education; for those aged 25 to 34, the rate of post-secondary education reached 51 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a> indicates that Canadian students perform well above the OECD average, particularly in mathematics, science, and reading.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadians</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden">
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:White"></div>
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 7957.328271171px; border-left-color:Black"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Black"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Black"></div>
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 2272.1757784946px; border-left-color:Red"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Red"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Red"></div>

<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div>
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 321.45820786341px; border-left-color:Gold"></div>
